	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Charlie Chaplin</h1>

	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>


		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">British comic actor and filmmaker</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Charles Chaplin" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Charles_Chaplin_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Charles Chaplin (disambiguation)">Charles Chaplin (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Sir Charles Spencer Chaplin</b> <span class="noexcerpt nowraplinks" style="font-size:100%;"><a href="/wiki/Knight_Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight Commander of the Order of the British Empire">KBE</a></span> (16 April 1889 ‚Äì 25 December 1977) was an English comic actor, filmmaker, and composer who rose to fame in the era of <a href="/wiki/Silent_film" title="Silent film">silent film</a>. He became a worldwide icon through his screen persona, "<a href="/wiki/The_Tramp" title="The Tramp">The Tramp</a>", and is considered one of the most important figures in the history of the film industry. His career spanned more than 75 years, from childhood in the Victorian era until a year before his death in 1977, and encompassed both adulation and controversy.
</p><p>Chaplin's childhood in London was one of poverty and hardship, as his father was absent and his mother struggled financially, and he was sent to a <a href="/wiki/Workhouse" title="Workhouse">workhouse</a> twice before the age of nine. When he was 14, his mother was committed to a <a href="/wiki/Mental_asylum" class="mw-redirect" title="Mental asylum">mental asylum</a>. Chaplin began performing at an early age, touring <a href="/wiki/Music_hall" title="Music hall">music halls</a> and later working as a stage actor and comedian. At 19, he was signed to the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Fred_Karno" title="Fred Karno">Fred Karno</a> company, which took him to America. He was scouted for the film industry and began appearing in 1914 for <a href="/wiki/Keystone_Studios" title="Keystone Studios">Keystone Studios</a>. He soon developed the Tramp persona and formed a large fan base. He directed his own films and continued to hone his craft as he moved to the <a href="/wiki/Essanay_Studios" title="Essanay Studios">Essanay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Film" title="Mutual Film">Mutual</a>, and <a href="/wiki/First_National_Pictures" title="First National Pictures">First National</a> corporations. By 1918, he was one of the best-known figures in the world.
</p><p>In 1919, Chaplin co-founded the distribution company <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a>, which gave him complete control over his films. His first feature-length film was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kid_(1921_film)" title="The Kid (1921 film)">The Kid</a></i> (1921), followed by <i><a href="/wiki/A_Woman_of_Paris" title="A Woman of Paris">A Woman of Paris</a></i> (1923), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gold_Rush" title="The Gold Rush">The Gold Rush</a></i> (1925), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Circus_(1928_film)" title="The Circus (1928 film)">The Circus</a></i> (1928). He initially refused to move to sound films in the 1930s, instead producing <i><a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">City Lights</a></i> (1931) and <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Times_(film)" title="Modern Times (film)">Modern Times</a></i> (1936) without dialogue. He became increasingly political, and his first sound film was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Dictator" title="The Great Dictator">The Great Dictator</a></i> (1940), which satirised <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. The 1940s were a decade marked with controversy for Chaplin, and his popularity declined rapidly. He was accused of communist sympathies, and some members of the press and public found his involvement in a paternity suit, and marriages to much younger women, scandalous. An FBI investigation was opened, and Chaplin was forced to leave the United States and settle in Switzerland. He abandoned the Tramp in his later films, which include <i><a href="/wiki/Monsieur_Verdoux" title="Monsieur Verdoux">Monsieur Verdoux</a></i> (1947), <i><a href="/wiki/Limelight_(1952_film)" title="Limelight (1952 film)">Limelight</a></i> (1952), <i><a href="/wiki/A_King_in_New_York" title="A King in New York">A King in New York</a></i> (1957), and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Countess_from_Hong_Kong" title="A Countess from Hong Kong">A Countess from Hong Kong</a></i> (1967).
</p><p>Chaplin wrote, directed, produced, edited, starred in, and composed the music for most of his films. He was a perfectionist, and his financial independence enabled him to spend years on the development and production of a picture. His films are characterised by slapstick combined with pathos, typified in the Tramp's struggles against adversity. Many contain social and political themes, as well as autobiographical elements. He received an Honorary Academy Award for "the incalculable effect he has had in making motion pictures the art form of this century" in 1972, as part of a renewed appreciation for his work. He continues to be held in high regard, with <i>The Gold Rush</i>, <i>City Lights</i>, <i>Modern Times</i>, and <i>The Great Dictator</i> often ranked on lists of the greatest films of all time.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#1953‚Äì1977:_European_years"><span class="tocnumber">1.6</span> <span class="toctext">1953‚Äì1977: European years</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1889.E2.80.931913:_Early_years"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1889‚Äì1913:_Early_years">1889‚Äì1913: Early years</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_childhood_hardship">Background and childhood hardship</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg/220px-Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg/330px-Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="349" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_at_Hanwell.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seven-year-old Chaplin (middle centre, leaning slightly) at the <a href="/wiki/Central_London_District_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Central London District School">Central London District School</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pauper" class="mw-redirect" title="Pauper">paupers</a>, 1897</div></div></div>
<p>Charles Spencer Chaplin was born on 16 April 1889 to <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Chaplin" title="Hannah Chaplin">Hannah Chaplin</a> (born Hannah Harriet Pedlingham Hill) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Chaplin_Sr" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Chaplin Sr">Charles Chaplin Sr</a>. There is no official record of his birth, although Chaplin believed he was born at <a href="/wiki/East_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="East Street">East Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walworth" title="Walworth">Walworth</a>, in <a href="/wiki/South_London" title="South London">South London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson10_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson10-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> His parents had married four years previously, at which time Charles Sr. became the legal guardian of Hannah's illegitimate son, <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Chaplin" title="Sydney Chaplin">Sydney John Hill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson3‚Äì4,_19_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson3‚Äì4,_19-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> At the time of his birth, Chaplin's parents were both <a href="/wiki/Music_hall" title="Music hall">music hall</a> entertainers. Hannah, the daughter of a shoemaker,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson3_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson3-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> had a brief and unsuccessful career under the stage name Lily Harley,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson5‚Äì7_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson5‚Äì7-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> while Charles Sr., a butcher's son,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeissman200910_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeissman200910-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> was a popular singer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson9‚Äì10,_12_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson9‚Äì10,_12-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Although they never divorced, Chaplin's parents were estranged by around 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson13_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson13-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The following year, Hannah gave birth to a third son ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/Wheeler_Dryden" title="Wheeler Dryden">George Wheeler Dryden</a> ‚Äì fathered by the music hall entertainer <a href="/wiki/Leo_Dryden" title="Leo Dryden">Leo Dryden</a>. The child was taken by Dryden at six months old, and did not re-enter Chaplin's life for 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson15_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson15-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin's childhood was fraught with poverty and hardship, making his eventual trajectory "the most dramatic of all the rags to riches stories ever told" according to his authorised biographer <a href="/wiki/David_Robinson_(film_critic)" title="David Robinson (film critic)">David Robinson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinsonxv_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinsonxv-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin's early years were spent with his mother and brother Sydney in the London district of <a href="/wiki/Kennington" title="Kennington">Kennington</a>; Hannah had no means of income, other than occasional nursing and dressmaking, and Chaplin Sr. provided no financial support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson16_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson16-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As the situation deteriorated, Chaplin was sent to <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Workhouse" title="Lambeth Workhouse">Lambeth Workhouse</a> when he was seven years old.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> The council housed him at the <a href="/wiki/Central_London_District_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Central London District School">Central London District School</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pauperism" title="Pauperism">paupers</a>, which Chaplin remembered as "a forlorn existence".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin29_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin29-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He was briefly reunited with his mother 18 months later, before Hannah was forced to readmit her family to the workhouse in July 1898. The boys were promptly sent to <a href="/wiki/West_Norwood" title="West Norwood">Norwood</a> Schools, another institution for destitute children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson24‚Äì26_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson24‚Äì26-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatleft" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:left; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">

<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äú
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">I was hardly aware of a crisis because we lived in a continual crisis; and, being a boy, I dismissed our troubles with gracious forgetfulness.
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äù
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>‚Äî&#160;Chaplin on his childhood<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin10_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin10-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In September 1898, Hannah was committed to <a href="/wiki/Cane_Hill_Hospital" title="Cane Hill Hospital">Cane Hill</a> mental asylum ‚Äì she had developed a <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychosis</a> seemingly brought on by an infection of <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a> and malnutrition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeissman200949‚Äì50_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeissman200949‚Äì50-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> For the two months she was there, Chaplin and his brother Sydney were sent to live with their father, whom the young boys scarcely knew.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin15,_33_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin15,_33-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Charles Sr. was by then a severe alcoholic, and life there was bad enough to provoke a visit from the <a href="/wiki/National_Society_for_the_Prevention_of_Cruelty_to_Children" title="National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children">National Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Children</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson27_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson27-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin's father died two years later, at 38 years old, from <a href="/wiki/Cirrhosis" title="Cirrhosis">cirrhosis</a> of the liver.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson36_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson36-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hannah entered a period of remission but, in May 1903, became ill again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson27_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson27-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin, then 14, had the task of taking his mother to the infirmary, from where she was sent back to Cane Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson40_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson40-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He lived alone for several days, searching for food and occasionally sleeping rough, until Sydney ‚Äì who had enrolled in the Navy two years earlier ‚Äì returned.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeissman20096Chaplin71‚Äì74Robinson35_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeissman20096Chaplin71‚Äì74Robinson35-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Hannah was released from the asylum eight months later,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson41_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson41-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> but in March 1905, her illness returned, this time permanently. "There was nothing we could do but accept poor mother's fate", Chaplin later wrote, and she remained in care until her death in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin88Robinson55‚Äì56_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin88Robinson55‚Äì56-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_performer">Young performer</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_in_Sherlock_Holmes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Chaplin_in_Sherlock_Holmes.jpg/170px-Chaplin_in_Sherlock_Holmes.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Chaplin_in_Sherlock_Holmes.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_in_Sherlock_Holmes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A teenage Chaplin in the play <i><a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes_(play)" title="Sherlock Holmes (play)">Sherlock Holmes</a></i>, in which he appeared between 1903 and 1906</div></div></div>
<p>Between his time in the poor schools and his mother succumbing to mental illness, Chaplin began to perform on stage. He later recalled making his first amateur appearance at the age of five years, when he took over from Hannah one night in <a href="/wiki/Aldershot" title="Aldershot">Aldershot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> This was an isolated occurrence, but by the time he was nine Chaplin had, with his mother's encouragement, grown interested in performing. He later wrote: "[she] imbued me with the feeling that I had some sort of talent".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin41_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin41-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Through his father's connections,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot4_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot4-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin became a member of the <a href="/wiki/The_Eight_Lancashire_Lads" title="The Eight Lancashire Lads">Eight Lancashire Lads</a> <a href="/wiki/Clog_dance" title="Clog dance">clog-dancing</a> troupe, with whom he toured English music halls throughout 1899 and 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin worked hard, and the act was popular with audiences, but he was not satisfied with dancing and wished to form a comedy act.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin44_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin44-35">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the years Chaplin was touring with the Eight Lancashire Lads, his mother ensured that he still attended school but, by age 13, he had abandoned education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish19_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish19-36">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson39_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson39-37">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He supported himself with a range of jobs, while nursing his ambition to become an actor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin76_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin76-38">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> At 14, shortly after his mother's relapse, he registered with a theatrical agency in London's <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a>. The manager sensed potential in Chaplin, who was promptly given his first role as a newsboy in <a href="/wiki/Harry_Arthur_Saintsbury" title="Harry Arthur Saintsbury">Harry Arthur Saintsbury</a>'s <i>Jim, a Romance of Cockayne</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson44‚Äì46_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson44‚Äì46-39">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It opened in July 1903, but the show was unsuccessful and closed after two weeks. Chaplin's comic performance, however, was singled out for praise in many of the reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot42‚Äì44Robinson46‚Äì47Louvish26_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot42‚Äì44Robinson46‚Äì47Louvish26-40">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Saintsbury secured a role for Chaplin in <a href="/wiki/Charles_Frohman" title="Charles Frohman">Charles Frohman</a>'s production of <i><a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes_(play)" title="Sherlock Holmes (play)">Sherlock Holmes</a></i>, where he played Billy the pageboy in three nationwide tours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson45,_49‚Äì51,_53,_58_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson45,_49‚Äì51,_53,_58-41">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> His performance was so well received that he was called to London to play the role alongside <a href="/wiki/William_Gillette" title="William Gillette">William Gillette</a>, the original Holmes.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> "It was like tidings from heaven", Chaplin recalled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin89_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin89-44">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> At 16 years old, Chaplin starred in the play's West End production at the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_York%27s_Theatre" title="Duke of York&#39;s Theatre">Duke of York's Theatre</a> from October to December 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot217_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot217-45">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He completed one final tour of <i>Sherlock Holmes</i> in early 1906, before leaving the play after more than two-and-a-half years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson63_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson63-46">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage_comedy_and_vaudeville">Stage comedy and vaudeville</span></h4>
<p>Chaplin soon found work with a new company, and went on tour with his brother ‚Äì who was also pursuing an acting career ‚Äì in a <a href="/wiki/Sketch_comedy" title="Sketch comedy">comedy sketch</a> called <i>Repairs</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson63‚Äì64_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson63‚Äì64-47">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In May 1906, Chaplin joined the juvenile act Casey's Circus,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot71_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot71-48">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> where he developed popular <a href="/wiki/Burlesque" title="Burlesque">burlesque</a> pieces and was soon the star of the show. By the time the act finished touring in July 1907, the 18-year-old had become an accomplished comedic performer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson64‚Äì68Chaplin94_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson64‚Äì68Chaplin94-49">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> He struggled to find more work, however, and a brief attempt at a solo act was a failure.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg/220px-Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg/330px-Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg/440px-Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="847" data-file-height="810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_Karno_advert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Advertisement from Chaplin's American tour with the <a href="/wiki/Fred_Karno" title="Fred Karno">Fred Karno</a> comedy company, 1913</div></div></div>
<p>Meanwhile, Sydney Chaplin had joined <a href="/wiki/Fred_Karno" title="Fred Karno">Fred Karno</a>'s prestigious comedy company in 1906 and, by 1908, he was one of their key performers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson71Kamin12Marriot85_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson71Kamin12Marriot85-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In February, he managed to secure a two-week trial for his younger brother. Karno was initially wary, and considered Chaplin a "pale, puny, sullen-looking youngster" who "looked much too shy to do any good in the theatre."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson76_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson76-53">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> However, the teenager made an impact on his first night at the <a href="/wiki/London_Coliseum" title="London Coliseum">London Coliseum</a> and he was quickly signed to a contract.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson76‚Äì77_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson76‚Äì77-54">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin began by playing a series of minor parts, eventually progressing to starring roles in 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot103,_109_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot103,_109-55">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In April 1910, he was given the lead in a new sketch, <i>Jimmy the Fearless</i>. It was a big success, and Chaplin received considerable press attention.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriot126‚Äì128Robinson84‚Äì85_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriot126‚Äì128Robinson84‚Äì85-56">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Karno selected his new star to join the section of the company, one that also included <a href="/wiki/Stan_Laurel" title="Stan Laurel">Stan Laurel</a>, that toured North America's <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville</a> circuit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson88_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson88-57">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The young comedian headed the show and impressed reviewers, being described as "one of the best pantomime artists ever seen here".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson91‚Äì92_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson91‚Äì92-58">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> His most successful role was a drunk called the "Inebriate Swell", which drew him significant recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson82Brownlow98_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson82Brownlow98-59">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The tour lasted 21 months, and the troupe returned to England in June 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson95_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson95-60">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin recalled that he "had a disquieting feeling of sinking back into a depressing commonplaceness" and was, therefore, delighted when a new tour began in October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin133‚Äì134Robinson96_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin133‚Äì134Robinson96-61">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1914.E2.80.931917:_Entering_films"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1914‚Äì1917:_Entering_films">1914‚Äì1917: Entering films</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Keystone">Keystone</span></h4>
<p>Six months into the second American tour, Chaplin was invited to join the New York Motion Picture Company. A representative who had seen his performances thought he could replace <a href="/wiki/Fred_Mace" title="Fred Mace">Fred Mace</a>, a star of their <a href="/wiki/Keystone_Studios" title="Keystone Studios">Keystone Studios</a> who intended to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson102_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson102-62">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin thought the Keystone comedies "a crude m√©lange of rough and rumble", but liked the idea of working in films and rationalised: "Besides, it would mean a new life."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin138‚Äì139_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin138‚Äì139-63">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He met with the company and signed a $150-per-week<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> contract in September 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson103Chaplin139_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson103Chaplin139-66">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin arrived in Los Angeles in early December,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson107_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson107-67">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and began working for the Keystone studio on 5 January 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Making a Living screenshot" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg/220px-Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg/330px-Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg/440px-Chaplin_Making_a_Living_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="413" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Chaplin (left) in his first film appearance, <i><a href="/wiki/Making_a_Living" title="Making a Living">Making a Living</a></i>, with Henry Lehrman who directed the picture (1914)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kid Auto Races at Venice screenshot" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg/220px-Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg/330px-Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg/440px-Chaplin_Kid_Auto_Races.jpg 2x" data-file-width="979" data-file-height="720" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/The_Tramp" title="The Tramp">The Tramp</a> debuts in <i><a href="/wiki/Kid_Auto_Races_at_Venice" title="Kid Auto Races at Venice">Kid Auto Races at Venice</a></i> (1914), Chaplin's second released film</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Chaplin's boss was <a href="/wiki/Mack_Sennett" title="Mack Sennett">Mack Sennett</a>, who initially expressed concern that the 24-year-old looked too young.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin141_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin141-69">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He was not used in a picture until late January, during which time Chaplin attempted to learn the processes of filmmaking.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson108_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson108-70">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Film_reel" class="mw-redirect" title="Film reel">one-reeler</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Making_a_Living" title="Making a Living">Making a Living</a></i> marked his film acting debut and was released on 2 February 1914. Chaplin strongly disliked the picture, but one review picked him out as "a comedian of the first water".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson110_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson110-71">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> For his second appearance in front of the camera, Chaplin selected the costume with which he became identified. He described the process in his autobiography:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I wanted everything to be a contradiction: the pants baggy, the coat tight, the hat small and the shoes large&#160;... I added a small moustache, which, I reasoned, would add age without hiding my expression. I had no idea of the character. But the moment I was dressed, the clothes and the makeup made me feel the person he was. I began to know him, and by the time I walked on stage he was fully born.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin145_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin145-72">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The film was <i><a href="/wiki/Mabel%27s_Strange_Predicament" title="Mabel&#39;s Strange Predicament">Mabel's Strange Predicament</a></i>, but "<a href="/wiki/The_Tramp" title="The Tramp">the Tramp</a>" character, as it became known, debuted to audiences in <i><a href="/wiki/Kid_Auto_Races_at_Venice" title="Kid Auto Races at Venice">Kid Auto Races at Venice</a></i> ‚Äì shot later than <i>Mabel's Strange Predicament</i> but released two days earlier on 7 February 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson113_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson113-75">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin adopted the character as his screen persona and attempted to make suggestions for the films he appeared in. These ideas were dismissed by his directors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson120_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson120-76">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> During the filming of his eleventh picture, <i><a href="/wiki/Mabel_at_the_Wheel" title="Mabel at the Wheel">Mabel at the Wheel</a></i>, he clashed with director <a href="/wiki/Mabel_Normand" title="Mabel Normand">Mabel Normand</a> and was almost released from his contract. Sennett kept him on, however, when he received orders from exhibitors for more Chaplin films.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Sennett also allowed Chaplin to direct his next film himself after Chaplin promised to pay $1,500 ($38,803 in 2019 dollars) if the film was unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson121_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson121-78">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Caught_in_the_Rain" title="Caught in the Rain">Caught in the Rain</a></i>, issued 4 May 1914, was Chaplin's directorial debut and was highly successful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson123_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson123-79">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Thereafter he directed almost every short film in which he appeared for Keystone,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland19895_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland19895-80">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> at the rate of approximately one per week,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaminxi_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaminxi-81">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> a period which he later remembered as the most exciting time of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin153_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin153-82">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin's films introduced a slower form of comedy than the typical Keystone farce,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson113_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson113-75">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and he developed a large fan base.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson125Maland19898‚Äì9_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson125Maland19898‚Äì9-83">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In November 1914, he had a supporting role in the first <a href="/wiki/Feature_length" title="Feature length">feature length</a> comedy film, <i><a href="/wiki/Tillie%27s_Punctured_Romance_(1914_film)" title="Tillie&#39;s Punctured Romance (1914 film)">Tillie's Punctured Romance</a></i>, directed by Sennett and starring <a href="/wiki/Marie_Dressler" title="Marie Dressler">Marie Dressler</a>, which was a commercial success and increased his popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson127‚Äì128_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson127‚Äì128-84">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> When Chaplin's contract came up for renewal at the end of the year, he asked for $1,000 a week ($25,869 in 2019 dollars) ‚Äì an amount Sennett refused as too large.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson131_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson131-85">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Essanay">Essanay</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg/220px-Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg/330px-Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="327" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_and_Purviance_in_Work.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chaplin and <a href="/wiki/Edna_Purviance" title="Edna Purviance">Edna Purviance</a>, his regular leading lady, in <i><a href="/wiki/Work_(1915_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Work (1915 film)">Work</a></i> (1915)</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Essanay_Studios" title="Essanay Studios">Essanay Film Manufacturing Company</a> of Chicago sent Chaplin an offer of $1,250 a week with a signing bonus of $10,000. He joined the studio in late December 1914,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson135_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson135-86">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> where he began forming a stock company of regular players, actors he worked with again and again, including <a href="/wiki/Leo_White" title="Leo White">Leo White</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bud_Jamison" title="Bud Jamison">Bud Jamison</a>, Paddy McGuire and Billy Armstrong. He soon recruited a leading lady ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/Edna_Purviance" title="Edna Purviance">Edna Purviance</a>, whom Chaplin met in a caf√© and hired on account of her beauty. She went on to appear in 35 films with Chaplin over eight years;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson138‚Äì139_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson138‚Äì139-87">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> the pair also formed a romantic relationship that lasted into 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson141,_219_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson141,_219-88">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin asserted a high level of control over his pictures and started to put more time and care into each film.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeibaur23Chaplin165Robinson140,_143_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeibaur23Chaplin165Robinson140,_143-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> There was a month-long interval between the release of his second production, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_Out_(1915_film)" title="A Night Out (1915 film)">A Night Out</a></i>, and his third, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Champion_(1915_film)" title="The Champion (1915 film)">The Champion</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson143_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson143-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The final seven of Chaplin's 14 Essanay films were all produced at this slower pace.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland198920_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland198920-91">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin also began to alter his screen persona, which had attracted some criticism at Keystone for its "mean, crude, and brutish" nature.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland19896,_14‚Äì18_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland19896,_14‚Äì18-92">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The character became more gentle and romantic;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland198921‚Äì24_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland198921‚Äì24-93">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tramp_(film)" title="The Tramp (film)">The Tramp</a></i> (April 1915) was considered a particular turning point in his development.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson142Neibaur23‚Äì24_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson142Neibaur23‚Äì24-94">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The use of pathos was developed further with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bank_(1915_film)" title="The Bank (1915 film)">The Bank</a></i>, in which Chaplin created a sad ending. Robinson notes that this was an innovation in comedy films, and marked the time when serious critics began to appreciate Chaplin's work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson146_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson146-95">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> At Essanay, writes film scholar <a href="/wiki/Simon_Louvish" title="Simon Louvish">Simon Louvish</a>, Chaplin "found the themes and the settings that would define the Tramp's world."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish87_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish87-96">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During 1915, Chaplin became a cultural phenomenon. Shops were stocked with Chaplin merchandise, he was featured in cartoons and comic strips, and several songs were written about him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson152‚Äì153KaminxiMaland198910_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson152‚Äì153KaminxiMaland198910-97">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In July, a journalist for <i><a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Magazine" title="Motion Picture Magazine">Motion Picture Magazine</a></i> wrote that "Chaplinitis" had spread across America.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland19898_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland19898-98">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> As his fame grew worldwide, he became the film industry's first international star.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish74Sklar72_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish74Sklar72-99">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> When the Essanay contract ended in December 1915,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson149_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson149-100">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin ‚Äì fully aware of his popularity ‚Äì requested a $150,000 signing bonus from his next studio. He received several offers, including <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Studios">Universal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Film" title="Fox Film">Fox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vitagraph_Studios" title="Vitagraph Studios">Vitagraph</a>, the best of which came from the <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Film" title="Mutual Film">Mutual Film</a> Corporation at $10,000 a week.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson156_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson156-103">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mutual">Mutual</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg/170px-Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg/255px-Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg/340px-Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg 2x" data-file-width="435" data-file-height="609" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlie_Chaplin_with_doll.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>By 1916, Chaplin was a global phenomenon. Here he shows off some of his merchandise, c. 1918.</div></div></div>
<p>A contract was negotiated with Mutual that amounted to $670,000 a year ($15.7 million today),<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> which Robinson says made Chaplin ‚Äì at 26 years old ‚Äì one of the highest paid people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson160_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson160-105">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The high salary shocked the public and was widely reported in the press.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarcher29_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarcher29-106">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> John R. Freuler, the studio president, explained: "We can afford to pay Mr. Chaplin this large sum annually because the public wants Chaplin and will pay for him."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson159_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson159-107">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mutual gave Chaplin his own Los Angeles studio to work in, which opened in March 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson164_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson164-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> He added two key members to his stock company, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Austin" title="Albert Austin">Albert Austin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Campbell_(actor)" title="Eric Campbell (actor)">Eric Campbell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson165‚Äì166_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson165‚Äì166-109">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and produced a series of elaborate two-reelers: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Floorwalker" title="The Floorwalker">The Floorwalker</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fireman_(1916_film)" title="The Fireman (1916 film)">The Fireman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Vagabond_(1916_film)" title="The Vagabond (1916 film)">The Vagabond</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/One_A.M._(1916_film)" title="One A.M. (1916 film)">One A.M.</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Count_(film)" title="The Count (film)">The Count</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson169‚Äì173_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson169‚Äì173-110">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> For <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pawnshop" title="The Pawnshop">The Pawnshop</a></i>, he recruited the actor <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bergman" title="Henry Bergman">Henry Bergman</a>, who was to work with Chaplin for 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson175_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson175-111">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Behind_the_Screen" title="Behind the Screen">Behind the Screen</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rink_(film)" title="The Rink (film)">The Rink</a></i> completed Chaplin's releases for 1916. The Mutual contract stipulated that he release a two-reel film every four weeks, which he had managed to achieve. With the new year, however, Chaplin began to demand more time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson179‚Äì180_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson179‚Äì180-112">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> He made only four more films for Mutual over the first ten months of 1917: <i><a href="/wiki/Easy_Street_(film)" title="Easy Street (film)">Easy Street</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cure_(1917_film)" title="The Cure (1917 film)">The Cure</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Immigrant_(1917_film)" title="The Immigrant (1917 film)">The Immigrant</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventurer_(1917_film)" title="The Adventurer (1917 film)">The Adventurer</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson191_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson191-113">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> With their careful construction, these films are considered by Chaplin scholars to be among his finest work.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownlow45Robinson191Louvish104Vance2003203_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownlow45Robinson191Louvish104Vance2003203-115">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>  Later in life, Chaplin referred to his Mutual years as the happiest period of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin188_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin188-116">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> However, Chaplin also felt that those films became increasingly formulaic over the period of the contract and he was increasingly dissatisfied with the working conditions encouraging that.
<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin was attacked in the British media for not fighting in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson185_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson185-118">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He defended himself, claiming that he would fight for Britain if called and had registered for the American draft, but he was not summoned by either country.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;k&#93;</a></sup> Despite this criticism Chaplin was a favourite with the troops,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson187_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson187-121">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and his popularity continued to grow worldwide. <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Weekly" title="Harper&#39;s Weekly">Harper's Weekly</a></i> reported that the name of Charlie Chaplin was "a part of the common language of almost every country", and that the Tramp image was "universally familiar".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson210_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson210-122">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In 1917, professional Chaplin imitators were so widespread that he took legal action,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson215‚Äì216_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson215‚Äì216-123">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and it was reported that nine out of ten men who attended costume parties dressed as the Tramp.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson213_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson213-124">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The same year, a study by the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Society_for_Psychical_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Society for Psychical Research">Boston Society for Psychical Research</a> concluded that Chaplin was "an American obsession".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson213_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson213-124">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The actress <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Maddern_Fiske" title="Minnie Maddern Fiske">Minnie Maddern Fiske</a> wrote that "a constantly increasing body of cultured, artistic people are beginning to regard the young English buffoon, Charles Chaplin, as an extraordinary artist, as well as a comic genius".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson210_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson210-122">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1918.E2.80.931922:_First_National"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1918‚Äì1922:_First_National">1918‚Äì1922: First National</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg/170px-Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg/255px-Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg/340px-Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1338" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Poster_-_A_Dog%27s_Life_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/A_Dog%27s_Life" title="A Dog&#39;s Life">A Dog's Life</a></i> (1918). It was around this time that Chaplin began to conceive the Tramp as "a sort of <a href="/wiki/Pierrot" title="Pierrot">Pierrot</a>", or sad clown.</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1918, Chaplin was visited by leading British singer and comedian <a href="/wiki/Harry_Lauder" title="Harry Lauder">Harry Lauder</a>, and the two acted in a short film together.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mutual was patient with Chaplin's decreased rate of output, and the contract ended amicably. With his aforementioned concern about the declining quality of his films because of contract scheduling stipulations, Chaplin's primary concern in finding a new distributor was independence; Sydney Chaplin, then his business manager, told the press, "Charlie [must] be allowed all the time he needs and all the money for producing [films] the way he wants&#160;... It is quality, not quantity, we are after."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson221_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson221-126">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In June 1917, Chaplin signed to complete eight films for <a href="/wiki/First_National_Pictures" title="First National Pictures">First National Exhibitors' Circuit</a> in return for $1&#160;million ($20 million today).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchickel8_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchickel8-127">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He chose to build his own studio, situated on five acres of land off <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard" title="Sunset Boulevard">Sunset Boulevard</a>, with production facilities of the highest order.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin203Robinson225‚Äì226_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin203Robinson225‚Äì226-128">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> It was completed in January 1918,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson228_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson228-129">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and Chaplin was given freedom over the making of his pictures.<sup id="cite_ref-BFI_first_national_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFI_first_national-130">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/A_Dog%27s_Life" title="A Dog&#39;s Life">A Dog's Life</a></i>, released April 1918, was the first film under the new contract. In it, Chaplin demonstrated his increasing concern with story construction and his treatment of the Tramp as "a sort of <a href="/wiki/Pierrot" title="Pierrot">Pierrot</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin208_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin208-131">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The film was described by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Delluc" title="Louis Delluc">Louis Delluc</a> as "cinema's first total work of art".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson229_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson229-132">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin then embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_bond#Sales_difficulties_and_the_subsequent_campaign" title="Liberty bond">Third Liberty Bond</a> campaign, touring the United States for one month to raise money for the Allies of the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson237,_241_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson237,_241-133">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He also produced a short propaganda film at his own expense, donated to the government for fund-raising, called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bond" title="The Bond">The Bond</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson244_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson244-134">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin's next release was war-based, placing the Tramp in the trenches for <i><a href="/wiki/Shoulder_Arms" title="Shoulder Arms">Shoulder Arms</a></i>. Associates warned him against making a comedy about the war but, as he later recalled: "Dangerous or not, the idea excited me."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin218_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin218-135">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> He spent four months filming the 45-minute-long picture, which was released in October 1918 with great success.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson241‚Äì245_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson241‚Äì245-136">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="United_Artists.2C_Mildred_Harris.2C_and_The_Kid"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Artists,_Mildred_Harris,_and_The_Kid">United Artists, Mildred Harris, and <i>The Kid</i></span></h4>
<p>After the release of <i>Shoulder Arms</i>, Chaplin requested more money from First National, which was refused. Frustrated with their lack of concern for quality, and worried about rumours of a possible merger between the company and <a href="/wiki/Famous_Players-Lasky" title="Famous Players-Lasky">Famous Players-Lasky</a>, Chaplin joined forces with <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Fairbanks" title="Douglas Fairbanks">Douglas Fairbanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Pickford" title="Mary Pickford">Mary Pickford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D._W._Griffith" title="D. W. Griffith">D. W. Griffith</a> to form a new distribution company ‚Äì <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a>, established in January 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin219‚Äì220Balio12Robinson267_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin219‚Äì220Balio12Robinson267-137">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The arrangement was revolutionary in the film industry, as it enabled the four partners ‚Äì all creative artists ‚Äì to personally fund their pictures and have complete control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson269_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson269-138">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin was eager to start with the new company and offered to buy out his contract with First National. They refused and insisted that he complete the final six films owed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin223_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin223-139">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg/170px-Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg/255px-Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg/340px-Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="472" data-file-height="673" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_The_Kid_2_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Kid_(1921_film)" title="The Kid (1921 film)">The Kid</a></i> (1921), with <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Coogan" title="Jackie Coogan">Jackie Coogan</a>, combined comedy with drama and was Chaplin's first film to exceed an hour.</div></div></div>
<p>Before the creation of United Artists, Chaplin married for the first time. The 16-year-old actress <a href="/wiki/Mildred_Harris" title="Mildred Harris">Mildred Harris</a> had revealed that she was pregnant with his child, and in September 1918, he married her quietly in Los Angeles to avoid controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson246_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson246-140">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, the pregnancy was found to be false.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson248_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson248-141">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin was unhappy with the union and, feeling that marriage stunted his creativity, struggled over the production of his film <i><a href="/wiki/Sunnyside_(film)" title="Sunnyside (film)">Sunnyside</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson246‚Äì249Louvish141_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson246‚Äì249Louvish141-142">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Harris was by then legitimately pregnant, and on 7 July 1919, gave birth to a son. Norman Spencer Chaplin was born malformed and died three days later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson251_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson251-143">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The marriage ended in April 1920, with Chaplin explaining in his autobiography that they were "irreconcilably mismated".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin235Robinson259_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin235Robinson259-144">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Losing the child, plus his own childhood experiences, are thought to have influenced Chaplin's next film, which turned the Tramp into the caretaker of a young boy.<sup id="cite_ref-BFI_first_national_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFI_first_national-130">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson252Louvish148_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson252Louvish148-145">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> For this new venture, Chaplin also wished to do more than comedy and, according to Louvish, "make his mark on a changed world."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish146_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish146-146">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Filming on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kid_(1921_film)" title="The Kid (1921 film)">The Kid</a></i> began in August 1919, with four-year-old <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Coogan" title="Jackie Coogan">Jackie Coogan</a> his co-star.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson253_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson253-147">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Kid</i> was in production for nine months until May 1920 and, at 68 minutes, it was Chaplin's longest picture to date.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson261_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson261-148">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Dealing with issues of poverty and parent‚Äìchild separation, <i>The Kid</i> was one of the earliest films to combine comedy and drama.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin233‚Äì234_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin233‚Äì234-149">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> It was released in January 1921 with instant success, and, by 1924, had been screened in over 50 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson265_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson265-150">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin spent five months on his next film, the two-reeler <i><a href="/wiki/The_Idle_Class" title="The Idle Class">The Idle Class</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson269_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson269-138">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Following its September 1921 release, he chose to return to England for the first time in almost a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson282_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson282-151">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> He then worked to fulfil his First National contract, releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Pay_Day_(1922_film)" title="Pay Day (1922 film)">Pay Day</a></i> in February 1922. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pilgrim_(1923_film)" title="The Pilgrim (1923 film)">The Pilgrim</a></i> ‚Äì his final short film ‚Äì was delayed by distribution disagreements with the studio, and released a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson295‚Äì300_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson295‚Äì300-152">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1923.E2.80.931938:_Silent_features"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1923‚Äì1938:_Silent_features">1923‚Äì1938: Silent features</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A_Woman_of_Paris_and_The_Gold_Rush"><i>A Woman of Paris</i> and <i>The Gold Rush</i></span></h4>
<p>Having fulfilled his First National contract, Chaplin was free to make his first picture as an independent producer. In November 1922, he began filming <i><a href="/wiki/A_Woman_of_Paris" title="A Woman of Paris">A Woman of Paris</a></i>, a romantic drama about ill-fated lovers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson310_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson310-153">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin intended it to be a star-making vehicle for Edna Purviance,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson302_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson302-154">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and did not appear in the picture himself other than in a brief, uncredited cameo.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson311‚Äì312_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson311‚Äì312-155">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> He wished the film to have a realistic feel and directed his cast to give restrained performances. In real life, he explained, "men and women try to hide their emotions rather than seek to express them".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson319‚Äì321_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson319‚Äì321-156">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> <i>A Woman of Paris</i> premiered in September 1923 and was acclaimed for its innovative, subtle approach.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson318‚Äì321_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson318‚Äì321-157">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The public, however, seemed to have little interest in a Chaplin film without Chaplin, and it was a <a href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Box office bomb">box office disappointment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish193_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish193-158">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The filmmaker was hurt by this failure ‚Äì he had long wanted to produce a dramatic film and was proud of the result ‚Äì and soon withdrew <i>A Woman of Paris</i> from circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson302,_322_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson302,_322-159">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg/220px-Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg/330px-Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg/440px-Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1452" data-file-height="1047" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_the_gold_rush_boot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Tramp resorts to eating his boot in a famous scene from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gold_Rush" title="The Gold Rush">The Gold Rush</a></i> (1925).</div></div></div>
<p>Chaplin returned to comedy for his next project. Setting his standards high, he told himself "This next film must be an epic! The Greatest!"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish195_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish195-160">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Inspired by a photograph of the 1898 <a href="/wiki/Klondike_Gold_Rush" title="Klondike Gold Rush">Klondike Gold Rush</a>, and later the story of the <a href="/wiki/Donner_Party" title="Donner Party">Donner Party</a> of 1846‚Äì47, he made what Geoffrey Macnab calls "an epic comedy out of grim subject matter."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKemp64Chaplin299_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKemp64Chaplin299-161">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gold_Rush" title="The Gold Rush">The Gold Rush</a></i>, the Tramp is a lonely <a href="/wiki/Prospecting" title="Prospecting">prospector</a> fighting adversity and looking for love. With <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Hale" title="Georgia Hale">Georgia Hale</a> as his new leading lady, Chaplin began filming the picture in February 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson337_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson337-162">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Its elaborate production, costing almost $1&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson358_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson358-163">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> included <a href="/wiki/Location_shooting" title="Location shooting">location shooting</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Truckee_Range" title="Truckee Range">Truckee mountains</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> with 600 extras, extravagant sets, and <a href="/wiki/Special_effect" title="Special effect">special effects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson340‚Äì345_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson340‚Äì345-164">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The last scene was shot in May 1925 after 15 months of filming.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson354_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson354-165">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin felt <i>The Gold Rush</i> was the best film he had made.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson357_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson357-166">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> It opened in August 1925 and became one of the highest-grossing films of the silent era with a U.S. box-office of $5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson358Kemp63_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson358Kemp63-167">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The comedy contains some of Chaplin's most famous sequences, such as the Tramp eating his shoe and the "Dance of the Rolls".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKemp63‚Äì64Robinson339,_353Louvish200Schickel19_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKemp63‚Äì64Robinson339,_353Louvish200Schickel19-168">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Macnab has called it "the quintessential Chaplin film".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKemp64_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKemp64-169">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin stated at its release, "This is the picture that I want to be remembered by".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVance2003154_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVance2003154-170">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lita_Grey_and_The_Circus">Lita Grey and <i>The Circus</i></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lita_Grey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lita_Grey.jpg/170px-Lita_Grey.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lita_Grey.jpg/255px-Lita_Grey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lita_Grey.jpg/340px-Lita_Grey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lita_Grey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lita_Grey" title="Lita Grey">Lita Grey</a>, whose bitter divorce from Chaplin caused a scandal</div></div></div>
<p>While making <i>The Gold Rush</i>, Chaplin married for the second time. Mirroring the circumstances of his first union, <a href="/wiki/Lita_Grey" title="Lita Grey">Lita Grey</a> was a teenage actress, originally set to star in the film, whose surprise announcement of pregnancy forced Chaplin into marriage. She was 16 and he was 35, meaning Chaplin could have been charged with <a href="/wiki/Statutory_rape" title="Statutory rape">statutory rape</a> under California law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson346_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson346-171">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> He therefore arranged a discreet marriage in Mexico on 25 November 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin_and_Vance53Vance2003170_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin_and_Vance53Vance2003170-172">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Their first son, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Chaplin_Jr." title="Charles Chaplin Jr.">Charles Spencer Chaplin, Jr.</a>, was born on 5 May 1925, followed by <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Chaplin_(American_actor)" title="Sydney Chaplin (American actor)">Sydney Earl Chaplin</a> on 30 March 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson355,_368_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson355,_368-173">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was an unhappy marriage, and Chaplin spent long hours at the studio to avoid seeing his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson350,_368_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson350,_368-174">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In November 1926, Grey took the children and left the family home.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson371_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson371-175">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> A bitter divorce followed, in which Grey's application ‚Äì accusing Chaplin of infidelity, abuse, and of harbouring "perverted sexual desires" ‚Äì was leaked to the press.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish220Robinson372‚Äì374_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish220Robinson372‚Äì374-176">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;l&#93;</a></sup> Chaplin was reported to be in a state of nervous breakdown, as the story became headline news and groups formed across America calling for his films to be banned.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson372‚Äì374Louvish220‚Äì221_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson372‚Äì374Louvish220‚Äì221-179">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Eager to end the case without further scandal, Chaplin's lawyers agreed to a cash settlement of $600,000&#160;&#8211;&#160;the largest awarded by American courts at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson378_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson378-180">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> His fan base was strong enough to survive the incident, and it was soon forgotten, but Chaplin was deeply affected by it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaland198999‚Äì105Robinson383_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaland198999‚Äì105Robinson383-181">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the divorce suit was filed, Chaplin had begun work on a new film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Circus_(1928_film)" title="The Circus (1928 film)">The Circus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson360_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson360-182">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> He built a story around the idea of walking a tightrope while besieged by monkeys, and turned the Tramp into the accidental star of a circus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson361_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson361-183">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Filming was suspended for 10 months while he dealt with the divorce scandal,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson371,_381_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson371,_381-184">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and it was generally a trouble-ridden production.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELouvish215_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELouvish215-185">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Finally completed in October 1927, <i>The Circus</i> was released in January 1928 to a positive reception.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson382_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson382-186">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1st_Academy_Awards" title="1st Academy Awards">1st Academy Awards</a>, Chaplin was given a special trophy "For versatility and genius in acting, writing, directing and producing <i>The Circus</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-circus_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circus-187">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Despite its success, he permanently associated the film with the stress of its production; Chaplin omitted <i>The Circus</i> from his autobiography, and struggled to work on it when he recorded the score in his later years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownlow73Louvish224_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownlow73Louvish224-188">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Lights"><i>City Lights</i></span></h4>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">

<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äú
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">I was determined to continue making silent films&#160;... I was a pantomimist and in that medium I was unique and, without false modesty, a master.
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äù
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>‚Äî&#160;Chaplin explaining his defiance against <a href="/wiki/Sound_film" title="Sound film">sound</a> in the 1930s<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin322_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin322-189">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>By the time <i>The Circus</i> was released, Hollywood had witnessed the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Sound_film" title="Sound film">sound films</a>. Chaplin was cynical about this new medium and the technical shortcomings it presented, believing that "talkies" lacked the artistry of silent films.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson389Chaplin321_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson389Chaplin321-190">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> He was also hesitant to change the formula that had brought him such success,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson465Chaplin322Maland200729_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson465Chaplin322Maland200729-191">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> and feared that giving the Tramp a voice would limit his international appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson389Maland200729_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson389Maland200729-192">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> He, therefore, rejected the new Hollywood craze and began work on a new silent film. Chaplin was nonetheless anxious about this decision and remained so throughout the film's production.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson389Maland200729_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson389Maland200729-192">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_City_Lights_still.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Chaplin_City_Lights_still.jpg/170px-Chaplin_City_Lights_still.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Chaplin_City_Lights_still.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="245" data-file-height="350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaplin_City_Lights_still.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">City Lights</a></i> (1931), regarded as one of Chaplin's finest works</div></div></div>
